    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17123593312180706771">Philip Latinowics is a successful but disillusioned painter who returns to his hometown on Croatia's Danubian plain after an absence of twenty-three years. He hopes that revisiting his cultural roots will inspire him to create the perfect work of art and thereby restore his faith in both art and life. Haunted by his troubled childhood, however, he falls in with shady chara</span>
  <span id="freeText17123593312180706771" style="display:none">Philip Latinowics is a successful but disillusioned painter who returns to his hometown on Croatia's Danubian plain after an absence of twenty-three years. He hopes that revisiting his cultural roots will inspire him to create the perfect work of art and thereby restore his faith in both art and life. Haunted by his troubled childhood, however, he falls in with shady characters and discovers the emotional, intellectual, and imaginative poverty of his background.</span>

<div id="review_3323692648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3323692648" />
    <a title="Nataša" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4994064-nata-a"><img alt="Nataša" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564211498p2/4994064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3323692648?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataša" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataša" href="/user/show/4994064-nata-a">Nataša</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3323692648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17330728953473343551">Pročitah li negde da Krleža važi za ženomrsca?<br/><br/>Ovo mi je tek drugi susret s njim (Glembajevih se više i ne sećam), tako da neću donositi zaključke u korist ili protiv gorenavadene tvrdnje - reći ću samo da sam mišljenja da je u ovom delu muška priroda u mnogo većoj meri "ojađena" no ženska.<br/><br/>Iako su obe protagonistkinje okaraterisane kao promiskuitetne i žene sumnjivog morala, mizoginija ne može značajnije ni doći do izražaja, od čemera i patetike pripisane muškim likovima - barem su moje impresije</span>
  <span id="freeText17330728953473343551" style="display:none">Pročitah li negde da Krleža važi za ženomrsca?<br /><br />Ovo mi je tek drugi susret s njim (Glembajevih se više i ne sećam), tako da neću donositi zaključke u korist ili protiv gorenavadene tvrdnje - reći ću samo da sam mišljenja da je u ovom delu muška priroda u mnogo većoj meri "ojađena" no ženska.<br /><br />Iako su obe protagonistkinje okaraterisane kao promiskuitetne i žene sumnjivog morala, mizoginija ne može značajnije ni doći do izražaja, od čemera i patetike pripisane muškim likovima - barem su moje impresije takve..a možda sam samo još uvek pod utiskom Hamsunovog Nagela...<br /><br />Da sumiram - beše ovo poprilično kilavo čitanje, bez nekog užitka....gubila sam se u dugim rečenicama, koncentracija nula bodova, mukotrpni monolozi...sve to me je dotuklo i jedva se "dovukoh" do poslednjih 20ak stranica, kada je nešto i počelo da se dešava...<br />...što opet ne znači da je roman loš, već samo da mi nije baš po ukusu. Toliko.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17330728953473343551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Jovan Autonomašević" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jovan Autonomašević" href="/user/show/69438797-jovan-autonoma-evi">Jovan Autonomašević</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9531505705" href="/book/show/2541127.Povratak_Filipa_Latinovicza">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096582859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356673219725238161">A curious but classic book, which I've read twice. An artist returns home after 20 years abroad, to face up to the personal demons that send him into exile in the first place. It's a trip into the stifling and stuffy world of provincial Habsburg aristocracy, their endless intrigues, backbiting, and attempts to move up the foodchain and avoid the fate worse than death - having to work for a living. How such a society is ultimately doomed to self-destruction, and how hard it is for anyone born int</span>
  <span id="freeText8356673219725238161" style="display:none">A curious but classic book, which I've read twice. An artist returns home after 20 years abroad, to face up to the personal demons that send him into exile in the first place. It's a trip into the stifling and stuffy world of provincial Habsburg aristocracy, their endless intrigues, backbiting, and attempts to move up the foodchain and avoid the fate worse than death - having to work for a living. How such a society is ultimately doomed to self-destruction, and how hard it is for anyone born into it to live a normal life without emigrating. We see this world through the artist's eye, as despite himself he is constantly inspired by the coarse world around him to create new paintings, that capture the rawness of country life and elevate it to the eternal. Interesting parallels with today's HDZ, the dominant political party in Croatia since the war, and a haven for the unscrupulously ambitious. Croatia is also undergoing a demographic crisis as young people leave in droves for the more established EU countries (as they are from the rest of the Balkans). Go west! Very well written, long and complex sentences ensnare and suffocate the reader in the moribund world described by the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356673219725238161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1528785294" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528785294" />
    <a title="Vatroslav Herceg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43488455-vatroslav-herceg"><img alt="Vatroslav Herceg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582541627p2/43488455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528785294?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vatroslav Herceg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vatroslav Herceg" href="/user/show/43488455-vatroslav-herceg">Vatroslav Herceg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528785294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10423116512817706305">Nedorađeno i zapravo nedovršeno djelo. Primjerice prebrzo se odvija zbližavanje Bobočke i Filipa. Sama Bobočka nije dovoljno psihološki produbljena. <br/>Lik rastrganog intelektualca i njegovu životnu sudbinu daleko bolje stvaraju, psihološki karakteriziraju Ulderiko Donadini ili Ivo Kozarčanin. <br/>Krleža je kao čovjek bio ljigavac koji se uvaljivao u guzicu moćnicima te je isključivo radi onoga što obični narod zove politika smatran tako dobar i cijenjen pisac.<br/>Žalosno je da se pored Donadinija ili Koza</span>
  <span id="freeText10423116512817706305" style="display:none">Nedorađeno i zapravo nedovršeno djelo. Primjerice prebrzo se odvija zbližavanje Bobočke i Filipa. Sama Bobočka nije dovoljno psihološki produbljena. <br />Lik rastrganog intelektualca i njegovu životnu sudbinu daleko bolje stvaraju, psihološki karakteriziraju Ulderiko Donadini ili Ivo Kozarčanin. <br />Krleža je kao čovjek bio ljigavac koji se uvaljivao u guzicu moćnicima te je isključivo radi onoga što obični narod zove politika smatran tako dobar i cijenjen pisac.<br />Žalosno je da se pored Donadinija ili Kozarčanina uzdiže Krleža na tron hrvatske književnosti dvadesetog stoljeća. Još je žalosnije štovanje utemeljenih konvencija o tome tko je kvalitetan književnik a tko nije. Krleža je bio dobar pisac dakako, posebice se ističu Gospoda Glembajevi, no da je Krleža vrhunac naše književnosti dvadesetog stoljeća to je uistinu klimavo i to je ustanovljeno radi izvanknjiževnih razloga. Svi oni koji slijede mrtvace ili starine koji su pisali književne teorije su zapravo poput Krleže. Oni su poput Krleže u smislu da sami sebe guraju u već izgrađenu cjelinu umjesto da je ruše. Krležino dodvoravanje vlastima je u usklađenom odnosu s dodvoravanjem današnjih studenata, ili bilo koga uključenog u književnu teoriju i kritiku, s štovanjem već ustanovljenih književnih velikana. Prije svega mislim na činjenicu da svi studenti kroatistike koje ja znam nisu nikada ni čitali Donadinija te studenti općenito ne rade kritički svoje seminarske radove.<br />Donadini treba biti u srednjoškolskim čitankama a ne Krleža. Žalosno je da kolo vode ljudi poput Krleže, umrtvljeni i vrijedni mravi svoje kolonije, a ne ljudi puni života i sumnje poput Donadinija.<br />Tama jače sjaji nego svjetlost.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10423116512817706305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3229450302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3229450302" />
    <a title="Bruno" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97396628-bruno"><img alt="Bruno" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570964679p2/97396628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3229450302?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruno" href="/user/show/97396628-bruno">Bruno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789539858757" href="/book/show/15721395-povratak-filipa-latinovicza">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97396628-bruno?shelf=croatian-literature">croatian-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97396628-bruno?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97396628-bruno?shelf=20-best-croatian-novels">20-best-croatian-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97396628-bruno?shelf=djela-miroslava-krle%C5%BEe">djela-miroslava-krleže</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3229450302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4151826866966624700">Kada sam ju pročitao prvi put (četvrti razred srednje, nap.), bio sam iscrpljen i zbunjen, jer su većinu sadržaja činila opisivanja te rijetki i ''ispraznuti'' dijalozi. Tek sam kod posljednjih poglavlja probudio interes (scena u kojoj se Filip verbalno sukobljava sa majkom), ali tada je priča došla k kraju, bez ikakvog osjećaja zadvoljstva. Nakon što sam ponovno pročitao cijelu knjigu ove godine, moj se dojam promijenio na bolje, iako ne dovoljno da bi dobilo veću ocjenu. Ključni razlozi leže u</span>
  <span id="freeText4151826866966624700" style="display:none">Kada sam ju pročitao prvi put (četvrti razred srednje, nap.), bio sam iscrpljen i zbunjen, jer su većinu sadržaja činila opisivanja te rijetki i ''ispraznuti'' dijalozi. Tek sam kod posljednjih poglavlja probudio interes (scena u kojoj se Filip verbalno sukobljava sa majkom), ali tada je priča došla k kraju, bez ikakvog osjećaja zadvoljstva. Nakon što sam ponovno pročitao cijelu knjigu ove godine, moj se dojam promijenio na bolje, iako ne dovoljno da bi dobilo veću ocjenu. Ključni razlozi leže u antipatičnosti glavnog protagonista (kroz cijeli roman je nezadovoljan sa svime i svačime i smatra se žrtvom odgoja), nedostatku prave kulminacije na sve, što se dešava u radnji (izgleda kao gradnja pruge, bez jasne destinacije) i prekasnog uvođenja suprotstavljenih stavova u dijalozima, koji su interesantni, ali samo ako je čitatelj voljan proći preko 60% sadržaja od onoga što sam naveo u prvoj rečenici. Točno je da se roman bavi izražavanjem podsvijesti svih emotivnih reakcija koje su se u Filipu nakupljale godinama, ali kada se tomu pridoda povratak (kao glavna tema), identitet (nedostatak očinske figure), društveni odnosi i mjesto među ljudima, stvara se dojam da je previše kuhara u jednoj kuhinji. Razlog zašto je na listi 20 najboljih hrvatskih romana na mom popisu jest zbog generalne i stručne prihvačenosti čitatelja, iako smatram knjigu ''Na rubu pameti'' rafiniranijim djelom. Ovako je ''Povratak Filipa Latinovicza'' ispao kao roman u začetku Krležinog proznog stvaralaštva, iako to nije točno. Jedino što mogu savjetovati čitatelju jest da bude strpljiv (strpljenje je vrlina vladara), ako pokaže interes da uzme ovu knjigu u svoje ruke.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4151826866966624700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3216502773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3216502773" />
    <a title="Bojana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110217880-bojana"><img alt="Bojana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3216502773?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bojana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bojana" href="/user/show/110217880-bojana">Bojana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9531505705" href="/book/show/2541127.Povratak_Filipa_Latinovicza">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3216502773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13777624550160396332">Svitalo je, kada je Filip stigao na kaptolski kolodvor. Dvadeset i tri godine nije ga zapravo bilo u ovom zakutku...<br/>Priča o povratku... povratku „kući“, u panonsko blato i gnjilu stvarnost tog podneblja, povratku detinjstvu i korenima, povratku majci i sebi...<br/>Godine između, ostaće za nas, čitaoce, kao progutane, u skoro potpunom mraku, tek nagoveštene...<br/>Filip Latinović, slikar, sada već u četrdesetim godinama, vraća se u svoj rodni kraj. Rastrzan, mučen pitanjima, u jeku krize sopstvenog stvaral</span>
  <span id="freeText13777624550160396332" style="display:none">Svitalo je, kada je Filip stigao na kaptolski kolodvor. Dvadeset i tri godine nije ga zapravo bilo u ovom zakutku...<br />Priča o povratku... povratku „kući“, u panonsko blato i gnjilu stvarnost tog podneblja, povratku detinjstvu i korenima, povratku majci i sebi...<br />Godine između, ostaće za nas, čitaoce, kao progutane, u skoro potpunom mraku, tek nagoveštene...<br />Filip Latinović, slikar, sada već u četrdesetim godinama, vraća se u svoj rodni kraj. Rastrzan, mučen pitanjima, u jeku krize sopstvenog stvaralaštva i identiteta, on kreće putem sećanja i prvodoživljenih slika (koje su po pravilu traumatične). Nejasan, skoro nikakav odnos sa majkom, nad kojim je neprestano visilo neizgovoreno pitanje ko mu je zapravo otac, obeležiće skoro čitav njegov život.<br />Rastočen kao i boje oko njega, nemoćan da u svoje slike utka i miris i zvuk doživljenog, izgubljen i otuđen, Filip hoda alejama sećanja u nadi da će tu pronaći odgovore kako pripadati, kako se povezati.<br />Kako je samo Krleža maestralnom strukturom romana, neobičnim uglovima naracije, dočarao ovo odisejsko putovanje, ovu potragu za smislom i inspiracijom. Razvio je on pred nas svoje platno i slikao, oštro povlačio poteze kistom ostavljajući nas bez daha. Kao da boravite u neverovatnoj galeriji, u kojoj umetnici pred publikom stvaraju svoja dela.<br />Ta nikad naslikana slika iz rane Filipove mladosti, koja je tragično formirala njegov tuluzlotrekovski odnos prema ženama, progoniće ga čitavog života. Pokrenut nejasnim, podsvesnim motivima i žudnjama mladog tela Filip odlazi u posetu frajlama, tim, za njega, mističnim bićima. Susret sa jednom od njih, u maloj, memljivoj sobi rodio je tu grotesknu sliku, sliku trbuha.<br />...ležala je žena, a trbuh joj je bio raskriven, ogroman i sasvim bjel kao svježi hljeb, kada leži na pekarskoj lopati.<br />Taj trbuh bi trebalo da se prelije preko platna u sasvim gnjilom, žitkom stanju... Jedno bijelo golo telo trebalo bi naslikati, morbidno, suludo, perverzno, kao torzo zamočen u rasvjetu straha, nemira, groznice, malodobne strave, tmine, smrada, bordelskog vonja kiselih perina...<br />Ali kako naslikati taj promukli ženski alt, koji je doznavši čiji je on mali, o njegovoj majci govorio kao da se radi o nekoj osobi koja se ne razlikuje od ostalih koje može naći u tim mračnim sobama? Kako dočarati da je pod tim golim trbuhom ostala oskvrnuta i zaklana jedna dečja duša?<br />*<br />Kako naslikati tu grotesknu simultanost koju je doživeo nakon povratka, na dan svetog Roka? Ispred crkve svetina ždere, pije, neki momci tuku staru grbavu prosjakinju, pijane žene podvriskuju, svi u orkestraciji razvratnog i đavolskog, a iznad oltara bleda, neupečatljiva slika Isusa.<br />Te ruke, te božanske, nadzemaljske pesnice treba da se uzdignu nad sve zemaljsko u nama, uzvitlane gnjevnim furiozom, kakav se javlja u mračnim oblačinama za ljetnjih predvečerja, kada se čuje daleka grmljavina pred potopom, kada se trese tlo pod nogama, i kada je to titansko, astralno, mramorno golo Kristovo tijelo jedini most po kome se može spasiti čovjek iz blata i smrada.<br />Hrist u visinama, a ispod ljudi u svom glibu i tavorenju, gnjili i krvavi, a između žene, golih trbuha, belih, presnih i naduvenih, koje su okrenule stražnjicu svemu što je zvezdano nad nama.<br />Ovo je samo delić ovog fenomenalnog romana. Bogat simbolima, pitanjima, slojevima, nemoguće ga je preneti, moguće je samo iskreno ga preporučiti.<br />Čitajte Krležu, veliki je!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13777624550160396332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230998758" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164701-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417977947p2/28164701.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230998758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15567253943654882445">Gledano u retrospekciji, ovaj roman se ne čini kao da bi bio loš. Naprotiv- povratak umjetnika kod kojeg je manjak volje i inspiracije doveo do preispitivanja identiteta i smisla života- čini se kao zanimljivo djelo. Pogrešno. Prateći vizualne, olfaktivne, taktilne i auditivne pjesničke slike koje nam je Krleža svojom prebogatom tehnikom deskripcije pokušao dočarati (moglo bi se reći da graniči s intelektualnim hvalisanjem), razvukao je radnju do te mjere da mi je među silnim, raskošnim opisima </span>
  <span id="freeText15567253943654882445" style="display:none">Gledano u retrospekciji, ovaj roman se ne čini kao da bi bio loš. Naprotiv- povratak umjetnika kod kojeg je manjak volje i inspiracije doveo do preispitivanja identiteta i smisla života- čini se kao zanimljivo djelo. Pogrešno. Prateći vizualne, olfaktivne, taktilne i auditivne pjesničke slike koje nam je Krleža svojom prebogatom tehnikom deskripcije pokušao dočarati (moglo bi se reći da graniči s intelektualnim hvalisanjem), razvukao je radnju do te mjere da mi je među silnim, raskošnim opisima sama potencijalna kvaliteta priče izgubila vrijednost. Uzmimo u obzir da je to prvi moderni hrvatski roman, no, čita se kao sporo-tempirani, pametno-pisani, povijesni roman koji većini današnjih čitatelja (čast časnim iznimkama) brzo dosadi.</span>

<div id="review_3491923925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3491923925" />
    <a title="Monty Milne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14797192-monty-milne"><img alt="Monty Milne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363450934p2/14797192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3491923925?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monty Milne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monty Milne" href="/user/show/14797192-monty-milne">Monty Milne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3491923925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15044182060231105629">When I heard this was considered one of the major works of Croatian literature I realised with a guilty start I had never read ANY Croatian literature. Now I have read this, my life feels a little less incomplete. So for that reason alone I’m glad I read it, but the experience was somewhat mixed.<br/><br/>I have to say that unlike a lot of novels this one gets better and better towards the end, and becomes very dramatic, with several alarming revelations and an ending of horrifying high drama. I also like</span>
  <span id="freeText15044182060231105629" style="display:none">When I heard this was considered one of the major works of Croatian literature I realised with a guilty start I had never read ANY Croatian literature. Now I have read this, my life feels a little less incomplete. So for that reason alone I’m glad I read it, but the experience was somewhat mixed.<br /><br />I have to say that unlike a lot of novels this one gets better and better towards the end, and becomes very dramatic, with several alarming revelations and an ending of horrifying high drama. I also liked the vivid descriptions, and the thought provoking treatment of art. Philip’s mother is upset at his portrait of her. So should art always strive to tell the truth? One feels many relationships would break down into anguished chaos if we always did.<br /><br />Philip mocks the limited intellectual horizons and artistic tastes of everyone else. The main effect of this is not to make them look stupid but to make him look arrogant and unpleasant. At one point he also strikes a woman – anyone who does this, in the pages of a novel or in real life, instantly forfeits my sympathy. The character of Dr Kyriales is confusing – is he a madman, a criminal, a liar? Perhaps all three? The discussions of metaphysics with him are extremely tedious and the dullest part of the book. <br /><br />So although there was much to enjoy here there was also quite a bit to dislike, and I also felt a little out of sympathy with Philip’s aesthetic sensibilities. He has a huge disdain for Habsburg baroque, whereas in an ideal world I would live surrounded by it. One can never have enough ormolu clocks and stucco cherubs, I find. And what was so great about the aesthetic that replaced it – the drear gritty proletarianism of Yugoslav communism? Grey concrete, terrible clothes, and tower blocks? No thanks….<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15044182060231105629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_467508040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467508040" />
    <a title="Pia Margić" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11923935-pia-margi"><img alt="Pia Margić" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509096192p2/11923935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467508040?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pia Margić" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pia Margić" href="/user/show/11923935-pia-margi">Pia Margić</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9531505705" href="/book/show/2541127.Povratak_Filipa_Latinovicza">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11923935-pia-margi?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11923935-pia-margi?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer467508040&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467508040" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10529830723649955355">HR; <br/>Povratak Filipa Latinovivza je klasično djelo hrvatske književnosti jednog od najpoznatijih autora, uvršteno u obveznu srednjoškolsku lektiru i državnu maturu.<br/>Iako teže za shvatiti, ne bi trebalo predstavljati problem tipičnom čitaču niti srednjoškolcu.<br/><br/>Djelo (čija je radnja u Hrvata opća kultura) za tematiku uzima život i dilemu jednog muškog lika koji predstavlja svoj život i odnos s majkom koja se predstavlja kao udovica njegova oca, iako je okolina ilitiga "komšiluk" vidi kao lokalnu kurt</span>
  <span id="freeText10529830723649955355" style="display:none">HR; <br />Povratak Filipa Latinovivza je klasično djelo hrvatske književnosti jednog od najpoznatijih autora, uvršteno u obveznu srednjoškolsku lektiru i državnu maturu.<br />Iako teže za shvatiti, ne bi trebalo predstavljati problem tipičnom čitaču niti srednjoškolcu.<br /><br />Djelo (čija je radnja u Hrvata opća kultura) za tematiku uzima život i dilemu jednog muškog lika koji predstavlja svoj život i odnos s majkom koja se predstavlja kao udovica njegova oca, iako je okolina ilitiga "komšiluk" vidi kao lokalnu kurtizanu. Filip svog oca nije nikada upoznao, no pri završetku djela možemo i sami vidjeti da on shvaća tko je taj čovjek bio.<br /><br />Filip u određenoj dobi bježi od kuće i probija se kroz život, te se vraća kako bi vidio svoju majku; koja tvrdi da ga ne pozna i tjera ga sa svoga praga, pri čemu možemo i sami osjetiti i doživjeti njegove osjećaje.<br /><br />Ovo je djelo doista klasik hrvatske pa čak i balkanske književnosti te bi ga svatko iole kulturan trebao pročitati i poznavati.<br /><br /><br />ENG; <br />The Return of Filip Latinovicz is a classic of croatian literature one of the most famous croatian authors, included in the mandatory high school reading list and state graduation program. Though harder to understand, it should not present a problem to a typical reader or a highschool student.<br /><br />This piece of literature (whose contet is common knowledge for the Croats) takes a subject of a male character that shows us his life, his dilemmas and his relationship with his mother, who presents herself as his fathers widow, though the neighbourhood sees her as a local courtesan. <br />Filip never met his father, but by the end of the story we can see that he understands who the man really was.<br /><br />At a certain age he runs away from home, fights his way through life and returnes home to see his mother; she refuses to open the door to a "stranger" and chases him away from her doorstep, and we can feel and live his emotions.<br /><br />This piece of literature is truly a classic of croatian, even balkanian literature and anyone even a little bit cultured should read and know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10529830723649955355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5042166954557563033">Krležina spisateljska vrijednost je neupitna, ima talent za pisanje, a i ova knjiga uvelike svjedoči o tome, ima u njoj izvarednih stvari, pa mislim kako se može reći za nju da je bitna i utjecajna. No, moram priznati kako mi je bila naporna za čitanje. Sve mi se sviđa, priča, kontekst, likovi, ali ne mogu reći kako sam uživala u čitanju.   <span id="freeText5042166954557563033" style="display:none">Krležina spisateljska vrijednost je neupitna, ima talent za pisanje, a i ova knjiga uvelike svjedoči o tome, ima u njoj izvarednih stvari, pa mislim kako se može reći za nju da je bitna i utjecajna. Po mom guštu nije posve, mada ne mogu odrediti što je to što mi nedostaje. Međutim ne bih rekla da je nezasluženo poznat, stvarno je zanimljiva priča.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer645518695830123667">Krleža's books would have been more interesting, if they were written in some other genre or style.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RAGjSE6bQ9mtMHYWStrLssgJitIhSbKHffgVZ9OHG6eusXld6gWeCGFw9KHoT4kHLuqFSFvZd/wcNvpVnyDL/Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('47QtnpDa6lntNW1dbe18gNiCd0oWQbT9f9D4wvcI2hAJBPeLNEQ3iCF17+rPeD41PmF40GzRcYYeHhfwu68KSg==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_11553583'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11553583-prokleta-avlija?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Prokleta avlija<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/2147.Ivo_Andri_?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Ivo Andrić<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.30 avg rating &mdash; 7,169 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1954\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer14058263970491405916\">Prokleta avlija/The Damned Yard (Description from Ivo Andrić Foundation website)\n\nThe novel is written in 1954. Ćamil, a wealthy young man of Smyrna living in the last years of the Ottoman Empire, is fascinated by the story of Džem, ill-fated brother<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14058263970491405916\" style=\"display:none\">Prokleta avlija/The Damned Yard (Description from Ivo Andrić Foundation website)\n\nThe novel is written in 1954. Ćamil, a wealthy young man of Smyrna living in the last years of the Ottoman Empire, is fascinated by the story of Džem, ill-fated brother of the Sultan Bajazet, who ruled Turkey in the fifteenth century. Ćamil, in his isolation, comes to believe that he is Džem, and that he shares his evil destiny: he is born to be a victim of the State. Because of his stories about Džem’s ambitions to overthrow his brother, Ćamil is arrested under suspicion of plotting against the Sultan. He is taken to a prison in Istanbul, where he tells his story, to Petar, a monk.\n\nOut of these exotic materials, Andrić has constructed a book of great clarity, brevity and interest. No doubt it will be read by some as a political parable about the tyranny of the State, but also as a quite simply story about ill-fortune and human misunderstanding, fear and ignorance. Džem and Ćamil are doomed – and the certainty of their persecution is sometimes relieved, sometimes intensified by the stupidity and fright of the people who cross their ill-starred lives.\n\nConstruction takes up most of the book’s space: the central story of Džem as related by Ćamil lasts only a chapter or two. For the rest of the time the reader strips layer off layer, as one narrator passes him on the next. There is an interesting passage that helps to explain this method, at the moment when Ćamil starts narrating Džem’s story in the first person. “I” is a word, we are told, which fixes the position of the speaker in such a way that the exercise of will is no longer possible, and the speaker strength is exceeded – strength, presumably, to break out of the identification that all his past actions and thoughts force upon him when he uses the word. “I” is both a confession and an imprisonment. The fact that the novel passes the reader on from one narrator to the next rather suggests that the author is taking constant evasive action, lest he betray himself or his reader into the kind of “personal confession” which seals the fate of Ćamil. What exactly this game of form flirting with meaning signifies, must be left to the individual reader.\n\nThe movement is centripetal, towards Džem’s story, and then disperses. Details within the story are made to mimic this form. Thus when Peter receives the message telling him of his impending release:\n\n“Two younger prisoners...were chasing around using him as the centerpoint of ever narrowing circles. Annoyed, he tried to break away from these exuberant youths when one of them brushed against him and he felt a folded scrap of paper thrust into his hand. The youths continued their chase but now in widening circles...”\n\nThe reader is led on just such a chase in the course of the novel. The effect of this is to make the plot seem more like a poetic image than an ordinary plot: capable, therefore, of as many meanings as are the images of an allusive poem. Yet the language is simple and direct, not at all “poetic”. The characters are remarkable alive, even in conversation. Karađoz, the governor of the goal, is a spidery authoritarian, who loves to torment the charges he loves. The prisoners “complained about the way one complains about one’s life and curses one’s destiny...it would have been hard for them to imagine life without him”.\n\n“The Devil’s Yard” is justified, as all symbolic and figurative novels must be, by the extent to which it touches the emotions. It is extremely moving. Fear, horror, despair, amusement at times – all these indicate that the threat of the meaning has been recognized.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14058263970491405916\" href=\"#\" It recounts the story of Sheikh Nuruddin, a dervish residing in an Islamic monastery in Sarajevo in the eighteenth century during the Ottoman Turk hegemony over the Balkans. When his brother is arrested, he must descend into the Kafkaesque world of the Ottoman authorities in his search to discover what happened to him. He narrates his story in the form of an elaborate suicide note, regularly misquoting the Koran. In time, he begins to question his relations with society as a whole and, eventually, his life choices in general. Hugely successful when published in the 1960s, Death and the Dervish is an enduring classic that was made into a feature length film in 1974.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"477798341506091906\" Zbirka je objavljena 1916. u izdanju Matice hrvatske, a drugo izdanje doživljava 1926.\n\nRadnju pokreću likovi iz pretkršćanske, slavenske mitologije, koje je Brlić-Mažuranić, inače i dvostruka kandidatkinja za Nobelovu nagradu za književnost, stilizirala davši im određene osobine. Posluživši se oblikom bajke i fantastičnim elementima, stvorila je autonomni svijet davnine u kojem se mitski svijet spaja sa secesijski stiliziranom slikom vremena, prostora, likova i događaja. Prvo izdanje je imalo šest priča, a u drugom izdanju su dodane još dvije.\n\nCroatian Tales of Long Ago (Croatian: Priče iz davnine), is a short story collection written by the acclaimed children\'s author Ivana Brlić-Mažuranić (sometimes spelled as &quot;Ivana Berlić-Mažuranić&quot; in English), originally published in 1916 in Zagreb by the Matica hrvatska publishing house. The collection is considered her masterpiece and it features a series of newly written fairy tales heavily inspired by motifs taken from ancient Slavic mythology of pre-Christian Croatia.\n\nCroatian Tales of Long Ago are seen as one of the most typical examples of her writing style which has been compared by literary critics to Hans Christian Andersen and J. R. R. Tolkien due to the way it combines original fantasy plots with folk mythology.
